Objectives:  
• Set up of pilot plant to recycle coated textiles and coated plastic parts for mechanical and for 
chemical recycling  
• Evaluation of the coating debonding systems using the pilot recycling lines   
• Validation of the pilot recycling lines using a well-defined waste stream of coated textile and plastic 
materials  
   Quality analysis of the recycled materials and evaluation of their potential use  
Description of work  
Task 4.1 Set-up and implementation of the recycling pilot line - AIMPLAS, CTECH, IVV, IRES, IRIS 
(M18-M33).   
Although in practice, the chemical and mechanical part can be combined, the so-called mechanical 
recycling line will be located at AIMPLAS and the so -called chemical recycling line at partner IVV . 
This is due to practical reasons: the chemical 
part cannot easily be transported and requires a non-explosive environment.  
Based on the results obtained in Tasks 2.3 and 2.4 and in WP3, this task will be focused on designing, 
implementing, controlling and optimizing the components of the recycling pilot plant.  
Subtask 4.1.1 Mechanical line.   
The following devices will be installed and adapted to set up the mechanical pilot recycling line:  
1) Optical sorting: to remove the non-suitable parts in the waste stream and to show the identification of the 
triggers  
2) Grinding: reduction of the size of the plastic parts for improving the efficiency of the activation system and 
for more easy feeding the waste into the centrifuge and the recycled plastics into the extruder,   
3) Activation: this is the unit where the triggers (IR, heat, MW) can be applied to loosen the (primer layer of 
the) coating to ease separation. The key activity here is the building of dedicated MW equipment: cavity 
design, selection of energy range, feeding system.  
4) Separation: actual physical separation of coatings and plastic parts. Two options: (i) ‘spinning’ the material 
in a high speed centrifuge – this is expected to be the most general technique; (ii) density separation for 
some material combinations like coatings on a TPU foam (for example the MBT use case).  
5) Melt pelletising: final extrusion step to obtain recycled pellets free of coatings to be reused for new 
applications. The melt extrusion process will be assis ted by Sc-CO2 cleaning technology for removal of 
VOCs and odors.  
In addition, IRIS will install the monitoring systems delivered in WP3 in the selected points of the recycling 
process for sorting and coating removal control. They will train AIMPLAS staff and attend the initial trials to 
verify the correct monitored results.  
Subtask 4.1.2 Chemical line.   
The plant (size of 10kg batches) will include a grinding unit, dissolution unit, a separation unit, that allows 
separating dissolved coating from undissolved substrates, as well as drying unit for both undissolved and 
dissolved materials and a final extruder incorporating degassing, which will produce recycled granules. If 
degasification problems occur, grinded materials from the separation units will be introduced in the 
AIMPLAS melt compounding unit with Sc-CO2 cleaning technology.  
Task 4.2 Activation system dependent process optimization (Creasolv, MW and IR) at laboratory 
level - IVV, AIMPLAS, CTAG, CTECH, NTUA (M18-M33).   
For each of the coated waste streams that we consider, a selection needs to be made to identif y which of 
the proposed debonding systems, developed in WP2, is the most suitable activation technology. This 
selection will be based on an analysis with respect to their effectiveness in activating the triggers in the 
distinct applications among different  materials. This needs to be done for the triggered mechanical and 
chemical type of recycling. This work builds further on the activities from WP2 (especially Tasks 2.2 and 
2.3) and will be implemented in interaction with Task 2.4. In other words: the lab-scale findings of WP2 will 
be upscaled and translated towards industrial equipment. The outcome of task 4.2 will be established 
processing parameters for the different activation systems.  
Smart plastic materials with intrinsic recycling properties by design  
Research & Innovation Action addressing CE-NMBP-26-2018  
  
[DECOAT]    Page 71 of 70  
This proposal version was submitted by GUY BUYLE on 28/06/2018 16:55:43 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Subm ission Service. 
Subtask 4.2.1 Mechanical line.   
Using tests specimens with coatings with various percentages of MW susceptors (prepared in WP2) and 
discontinuous laboratory MW and standard ovens, the capacity of the melting of the primer layer will be 
evaluated. With the help of a DoE methodology, the materials with susceptors will be subjected to different 
MW and heating doses (taking into account as main parameters of the equipment: frequency, voltage power 
and time of exposure). The increase of temperature of the specimen during the test will be monitored by an 
infrared camera. The objective is to reduce the time inside the oven to less than 5 minutes without matrix 
degradation. The goal is that the process does not modify the final properties of the matrix. The properties 
of removed coating material w ill be measured using DSC and/or TGA tests. The amount of remaining 
coating on the plastic part will be evaluated according to protocol defined in Task 2.2.2. The activation 
technologies will be characterised using parameters such as: not affecting the pro perties of the substrate 
material, residence time in the oven and the energy and materials required for the coating removal.   
Subtask 4.2.2 Chemical line.   
The Creasolv® Process will be used for a selective dissolution of coatings and for initial sample production. 
This may be done a) by dissolution of the coating itself, or b) in case of presence of a primer layer by 
dissolving that layer only. Whereas a) would allow a solid/liquid separation of dissolved coating from 
undissolved substrate directly, b) implies a subsequent separation of coating films from substrate matter. It 
is expected that coating material and substrate will exhibit differences in density, thu s separation of both 
after removing the primer layer will be performed by density separation in liquids exhibiting a density 
between the densities of both materials. This in order to obtain a stream with components that can be 
separated by density or other separation technologies. Dissolved coatings will be separated from the solvent 
and the solvent will be completely re-used in the  
process. The coating polymer will be recovered and evaluated for a suitable second life application in 
Task 4.4.  
Task 4.3 Validation of the recycling pilot line performance using well -defined waste streams made 
with flat testspecimens - AIMPLAS, IVV, MAIER, MBT, PANASONIC (M30-M39).   
The goal is to validate the two recycling pilot lines. For this purpose, specific test samples will be produced. 
The test samples will be a combination of coating material, triggerable additive and substrate. The task will 
validate the recycling pilot plan ts (mechanical at AIMPLAS and Creasolv at IVV) for at least two types of 
substrates (plastic object and textile fabric).   
Each of the defined process parameters will be optimized for each waste stream to minimize energy/material 
consumption per kilogram o f treated material and maximize the final properties of the final recycled 
products.   
Task 4.4 Maximising the application potential of the recycled materials - CTAG, AIMPLAS, 
PANASONIC, MAIER, MBT, 
IVV, CTB, NTUA (M30-M42)   
Here, we will characterise the recycled materials coming from Task 4.3. First, we need to determine the 
purity of the material, see also Task 2.2.2, to check if we get in the scaled up line the same levels as on 
smaller scale. Second, we need the classical characterisation to determine  the quality of the recycled 
materials and to determine the recycling yield, using the most suitable techniques (for example Electronic 
microscopy, DSC, DMTA, rheological tests, thermal behaviour, ageing behaviour). NTUA can support this 
task with: SEM/EDX , TGA, rheology measurements, hardness measurements, microCT analysis.  The 
purity of the substrate material will be investigated by specific analysis (microscopy, FTIR, DSC, REM). 
CTAG can test the recycled material following end -user standards: climate ageing, UV and IR resistance, 
resistance to different chemicals, fatigue, impact, tensile strength. The quality of the recycled materials will 
be determined following the suitable EN/ISO standards to assess if we are above or below the maximum 
level of damage that the coating can withstand and considering the different types of materials.   
On top of that, we will study the selection of suitable additives to upgrade the recycled polymer materials , 
eg by protecting from degradation during recycling with the g oal to widen their lifespan (e.g. thermal 
protection, antioxidants, compatibilizers, chain extenders, UV stability, etc.). For this, we will use the state-
Smart plastic materials with intrinsic recycling properties by design  
Research & Innovation Action addressing CE-NMBP-26-2018  
  
[DECOAT]    Page 72 of 70  
This proposal version was submitted by GUY BUYLE on 28/06/2018 16:55:43 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Subm ission Service. 
of-the-art at that moment as this is a field in full progress. The goal is to optimise the substrate material 
during recycling for maximising the circular use.  
Based on the characterisation and ‘upgrading’ of the recycled material, an analysis of the potential uses of 
the recycled materials will be done. This will depend on the purity of the materials we can get. This is crucial 
as the re-use of the recycled materials might not be necessarily for the same applications as the original 
one, but might be more suited for other applications. We will investigate that, making sure that these other 
applications go for the highest added value as possible.

Objectives: General objective is the demonstration of the circular use of coated parts via 
triggered debonding  
• Make prototype of a ‘circular coated part’ for at least 4 actual parts – one for 
each end-user 
   Demonstration of circular use for at least 1 plastics and 1 textile 
based part

Description of work:  
Task 5.1: Eco -design of use case products in view of project technological developments - MBT, 
MAIER, CTAG, PANASONIC, ECOMAT, VAUDE (M31-M42).  
Activities of this task aim at selecting the most appropriate materials and processing, among those 
developed in previous WPs, to be used for the manufacturing of the final prototypes. The primary selection 
criterion will be the level of compliance to the requirements of each end use case, as specified in WP1, both 
in terms of materials properties and in terms of production parameters. Interim results of the LCA, LCC and 
safety analysis (WP6) will also be considered as well as the updated intelligence on exploitation (WP7).   
Where needed a redesign of the (coating of the) part will be performed to make the recycling easier. This  
could mean for example the addition of a tie layer to introduce the required debonding adhesives or using 
a different type of coating material.  
The redesign will also have to take into account that materials need to be used that can go through several 
cycles of use.  
We will consider the full cycle of processes the parts / products need to go through. This means that based 
on the developments made in WP1 to WP4, the full value chain for making the product circular cycle 
will be made. This includes the use  of the debonding technology developed. That way, we will make a 
realistic assessment of the disassembly, the triggered mechanical recycling and/or the Creasolv recycling 
steps that will be needed to obtain the substrate material, and potentially also the coated material, again as 
a secondary raw material. If the initial requirements, defined in Task 1.1 can be met, the materials could be 
fully used for the same application again. In the case not all requirements can be fulfilled, the most likely 
scenario, alternative solutions will have to be sought, eg addition of virgin material, use of the materials for 
alternative but also high value applications, perhaps adding an extra cleaning/recycling step/…   
The outcome of this task will be a report describing for at least 8 material combinations (which will be 
based on the use case of the end users) the value chain and technologies to reach circularity. These 
8 cases will act as examples and the goal is to make this public, to inspire and stimulate external partners.  
Task 5.2: Manufacturing of prototypes - MAIER, MBT, CTAG, PANASONIC, AIMPLAS, CTB (M36 -
M46).   
Manufacturing of at least 4 prototypes , ideally one for each end -user (VAUDE, MAIER, DAIMLER, 
PANASONIC) to show the proof of principle for ‘circular’ use.   
The goal of the task is to show that products can be produced meeting the necessary requirements and that 
the coating can be removed. This means that apart from the actual coated part, (some of) the other parts of 
the product need to be made, to be able to show the full disassembly, decoating and recycling process.  
The goal is to manufacture these four prototypes out of the following list of the use cases, see section 2.1.2. 
Comprehensive testing will be done, according to the specifications of each pro totype, by the end -users 
(VAUDE, PANASONIC, MAIER and MBT) in collaboration with the RTD partners.  
Task 5.3 Implementation of circular use cases - AIMPLAS, MAIER, MBT, PANASONIC, CTAG, VAUDE 
(M39-M48).  
For at least two of the use cases (one for plastics substrate and one for textiles substrate), we will 
show ‘multiple circular use’ for a coated part. For showing this, we will use: (i) the pilot recycling developed 
in WP4; (ii) the optical sorting and monitoring systems developed in WP3. For the pilot plant recycling trials, 
Smart plastic materials with intrinsic recycling properties by design  
Research & Innovation Action addressing CE-NMBP-26-2018  
  
[DECOAT]    Page 74 of 70  
This proposal version was submitted by GUY BUYLE on 28/06/2018 16:55:43 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Subm ission Service. 
we aim for at least 10-15kg of material to be processed in a batch process. Given that the use case products 
we target (see section 2.1.2) typically weigh some kilograms, it implies that we aim for showing circularity 
on products sets o f some tens of pieces. We will focus on the debonding step, i.e. the so -called 2nd level 
(see also section 1.3(a)). Where also the 1st level, i.e. the disassembly, is needed, this will be done manually. 
Goal is to show the use of the materials for at least two cycles, with minimum addition of virgin material.   
Further, we want to show the circular use of two generic items : one coated textile and one coated 
(injection moulded) plastic part. For each of them, we will aim for at least 5 cycles of material use , with 
minimum addition of virgin material. This will require the selection of coating and substrate materials that 
allow being recycled. For these trials, we need to focus on material combinations (coating and substrate) 
that are able to go through several recycling cycles. For textiles, a logical candidate could be a PES fabric 
with a PVC or TPU coating. For plastics, an ABS substrate painted with PUR, epoxy or acrylic.  
Task 5.4 Evaluation & Guidelines for further industrial take-up – MAIER, MBT, PANASONIC, CTAG, 
IRES, VAUDE (M39M48).  
From the technical side, and with the help of WP6, the guidelines will include elements like which trigger to 
add to which coatings/substrates, practical debonding systems, set-up of recycling lines, recommendation 
for further scale up,…. Other aspects to be considered will be the practical handling of the materials (eg 
shelf life), safety aspects where needed,…   
This will help “production” and “marketing” to consider new strategies to promote the debondable coatings 
and to compensate for the anticipated (slightly) higher cost of the new DECOAT-based products.

Objectives:   
• Life cycle assessment (LCA) will analyse environmental aspects and impacts of product systems and 
will assess how the developed products and processes will affect the environment, and human health, 
in their life cycle perspective.   
• Cost evaluation: Economic and market analysis refers not only to the cost of the formed materials but 
also contains the wider implications of technology selection on company performance.   
• Risk assessment and Safe-by-Design (SbD) approach will be applied in the early stages of DECOAT 
project. During the R&D and design phases of the proposed technologies SbD approaches will be 
introduced and used as a result of a continuous evaluation.   
• Health risks assessment by performing in vitro toxicity tests.  
• An innovative eco -design tool will be developed to identify benefits and strategies to support the 
industrial sectors.   
Description of work:  
Task 6.1: Risk assessment & Safe-by-Design principles - IRES, NTUA & ALL PARTNERS (M1-M39).   
A Safe-by-Design approach will be applied in the early stages of DECOAT project and will emphasize on 
the decision making process regarding design, materials used and methods in order to enhance the safety 
of final products and con trol the related health risks. Safe -by-Design aims at addressing safety issues 
already during the R&D and design phases of the proposed technologies. Safe by Design approaches will 
be employed to minimise health hazards, environmental and economic impacts.  One of the key elements 
for establishing a safety management system and implementing Safe by Design principles into the DECOAT 
project, is to ensure that risks associated with hazards are evaluated and managed within acceptable safety 
requirements, via risk assessment techniques and methods. DECOAT project aims to set out specific duties 
applying to employers and manufacturers focusing on risks associated with the use of hazardous 
substances. Special attention will be given to the description of properties, health hazards, precautions for 
use (e.g. REACH) and safe handling of hazardous substances, providing vital information not only to the 
employers but also to end-users. Finally, the aim of this task is to supervise safety procedures at the early 
stage an d update them periodically while toxicological information received from Task 6.4 (from 
nanomaterials synthesis to the final disposal) becomes available.  
Task 6.2: Life Cycle Assessment - ECOMAT, IRES & ALL PARTNERS (M12-M46).   
Life cycle assessment studies will be implemented in order to evaluate the environmental impacts of the 
product systems incorporating the developed coatings and the respective recycling processes, as well as 
determine the environmental performance improvem ents of the suggested processes compared to the 
current end-of-life scenarios (landfilling or energy recovery). Life Cycle Assessment (LCA) is a structured, 
comprehensive and internationally standardised method for environmental impacts of product systems. LCA 
takes into consideration products’ full life cycle, beginning from the extraction of resources, continuing with 
the production, use, recycling and ending with the disposal of remaining waste. It is distinguished from other 
environmental assessment met hods by two unique features: the analysis from ‘cradle -to-grave’ and the 
‘functional unit’. Specific guidelines and standards, such as ISO 14040 and 14044, provide the 
indispensable framework for Life Cycle 
Assessment (LCA). DECOAT project will take advant age of this decision support tool, using commercial 
software, in order to 
develop competitive and sustainable innovative products.  
By M12 the four most prominent applications (coated material + coating) will be chosen for serving as a 
base for the assessment within the project as case study parts (1 coated textile, 1 coated electronics part, 
2 automotive parts). The assessment of environmental impacts of the product systems will be based on the 
functional units of a service provided by a respective part to the main end user over a period of one year.  
The assessments will run from M12 on and in the beginning (estimated TRL3 -TRL4) would include 
screening LCA studies with identification of the hotspots for the materials and production choices at the 
moment of assessments on the laboratory or experimental scale, as well as the assessment of the base 
level product systems scenari os. These will make a significant contribution to the development of the 
technology, incorporating eco -design strategies to the product development. Once the technology 
Smart plastic materials with intrinsic recycling properties by design  
Research & Innovation Action addressing CE-NMBP-26-2018  
  
[DECOAT]    Page 76 of 70  
This proposal version was submitted by GUY BUYLE on 28/06/2018 16:55:43 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Subm ission Service. 
development reaches the point of a reasonable certainty about the production processes (TRL5) and allows 
to decide about the type of coating material and product recycling technology for each of the trial parts, a 
full LCA will be implemented. As a result, four full LCA studies will be reported covering each of the study 
case part with the c hosen coating material and recycling technology. Sensitivity analysis is to be 
implemented for the final full LCA studies in order to evaluate the performance from the perspectives of 
different scenarios of the products’ future, and to validate the improvements independently on the analyses 
methodological choices. Special attention will be paid to evaluation of the impact of methodological choices 
regarding the product systems’ end -of-life, including landfilling, incineration, bulk material recycling, and 
coating material recycling.  
Data collection will be conducted continuously throughout the project. It will include regularly primary data 
collection for the processes under investigation with involvement of technical experts in workshops and 
questionnaires and supported by the secondary data collection with use of internationally recognised 
databases, including specialized on the process data in coating industry.   
Task 6.3 Life Cycle Costing - IRES, NTUA, ECOMAT & ALL PARTNERS (M18-M46).  
Life Cycle Costing (LCC) is an assessment of all costs related to a product or service, over the entire life 
cycle, from production over use until disposal. IRES will combine LCC with LCA in order to provide a holistic 
approach regarding Life Cycle Cost. This combination w ill lead to the estimation and the same time 
minimisation of the economic impact arising from the applied processes and the material used. As a general 
pillar of this WP economic analysis will include material costs, manufacturing costs, operation costs an d 
maintenance costs of developed multifunctional systems. A comparison among all these costs, regarding 
DECOAT’s innovative materials and traditional ones, will be made. Main focus of this task will be the 
economic sustainability and the competitiveness of  both the final materials and the developed processes. 
In this framework, LCC will be applied in order to ensure that the evolution of the produced materials will be 
evaluated on time to match with the commercial life of recycling products. In addition, issues related to the 
evolution that technology and the market can be submitted, giving a competitive advantage that will boost 
the EU’s circular economy. Thus, the economic analysis which will take place into DECOAT project refers 
not only to the cost of ma terials and manufacturing but also includes the wider implications of technology 
selection on project’s performance.  
Task 6.4 Toxicity, Release and Exposure assessment - NTUA, IRES, CTB, AIMPLAS, CTAG, CTB, IVV 
(M6-M39).   
Due to that fact that safe by design always includes a compromise between functionality and safety, residual 
health risks cannot be excluded in DECOAT proposal, where a variety of nanomaterials is synthesized in 
WP1. In this task, this residual health risk will be assessed by performing in vitro toxicity tests initially on the 
developed hybrid nanomaterials, which have not been extensively studied. Moreover, release tests will be 
executed to the final formulations and representative specimens, to ensure that the nanomaterials are 
embedded in the adhesives, without any risk of mitigation. Finally, exposure assessment will be conducted 
to identify, characterise and quantify releases in the recycling processing activities (WP4) that may present 
an exposure risk, through open source software. The activities undertaken will allow the development of 
best practice risk management, to minimise and control the health risks for researchers, manufacturers and 
end-users involved with the project.  
Task 6.5 Eco-design tool - ECOMAT, IRES, OSM (M12-M46).  
To make use of the results of the assessments of the WP6, and to facilitate dissemination of DECOAT 
technological solutions,  
Task 6.5 will develop an eco-design tool for benefits and strategies identification. The tool aims to support 
the industrial sectors (both Project partners and external parties) to identify eco -design strategies for new 
products based on the DECOAT solutions (qualitative module), as well as to quantify the benefits of using 
the DECOAT solutions in their businesses (quantitative module). To increase accessibility of the tool, it will 
be developed in the form of a web tool available for use by the external parties at the website of the DECOAT 
project. The scope will focus on one generic combination of a coated material and a coating solution, and 
thus would be applicable to multiple products within different sectors. The exact materials and coatings will 
Smart plastic materials with intrinsic recycling properties by design  
Research & Innovation Action addressing CE-NMBP-26-2018  
  
[DECOAT]    Page 77 of 70  
This proposal version was submitted by GUY BUYLE on 28/06/2018 16:55:43 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Subm ission Service. 
be identified and selected in M12 based on the preliminary assessment results on the most prominent and 
elaborated combination.  
The tool will be developed in three main stages. At the first stage (M12-M18) internal and external research 
will be implemented  
to identify the functionality o f the tool and the scope of the required output information. At the end of the 
stage, the conceptual design of the tool will be developed, including structure, features and functionality. 
The second stage (M19 -M36) will focus on translating the conceptual design into a qualitative and 
quantitative assessment tool with the main purpose of communicating the tangibility of DECOAT results. As 
this stage the basic architecture of the tool will be developed. The tool will exploit first the preliminary 
screening LCA results, and will be digitalised as a web-based tool that went through technical and functional 
testing. The qualitative outputs will identify the main user’s opportunities to benefit from including DECOAT 
solutions into own product design or value chain. At the final stage (M24 – M48) the tool will be adjusted to 
the quantitative higher certainty results of full LCA and LCC studies, incorporating the qualitative 
assessment of the potential benefits to exploit the DECOAT solutions.

Description of work:  
Task 7.1 Update and evaluation of outreach strategy - CTB, OSM, ISWA, ECOMAT, ALL PARTNERS 
(M1-M48).  
The goal of this task is to extend the initial PEDR and to have a first more detailed plan, collecting input 
from ALL partners, by M6. Afterwards, the PEDR will be regularly (i.e. 12-monthly) updated, ad hoc updates 
will be done as needed. This frequent updating is considered needed for optimising the activities among 
the partnership.  
When implementing our outreach activities, we will focus on 3 main areas:  
(i) exploitation & technology transfer, preparing for further (industrial) uptake and leveraging of DECOAT 
outcome  
(ii) dissemination to ‘peers’ and wider stakeholder community  
(iii) communication to EU citizens – waste & recycling, especially of the thematic of textiles and 
plastics recycling as this topic is ‘living’ among the wider public in several European countries. Via 
DECOAT we want to convey the message that science and technology can bring valuable solutions for 
environmental issues (and is not only causing them).  
Within the PEDR we will also include evaluation activities: at least yearly, and also after major events (eg 
after press release or an event).   
Task 7.2: Exploitation and technology transfer - OSM, ECOMAT, ALL partners (M1-M48).   
Exploitation activities  will cover the assessment of the market and of the exploitation/business 
potential by the SMEs and the industrial partners. It will start with a cost benefit analysis identifying its 
particular possibilities for production and commercialization. The exploitation plan will study in detail the 
different exploitation strategies for the project outcomes and those to be involved after the end of DECOAT. 
Major input to the effort will be provided by the SME and industry partners involved in 
the technical and economic aspects. Barriers that may prevent the market penetration (see also section 
2.1.4) of the DECOAT solutions into the manufacturing industry will be identified and strategies to overcome 
them outlined. The industrial partners will further develop preliminary business plans for the relevant 
DECOAT outcome, elaborating the preliminary draft plans for exploitation provided at proposal stage (see 
section D2 of the PEDR). Such updates will be done at M18, M36 and M48.  
Throughout the project the Exploitation and Innovation Manager (EIM, see also section 3.2.1.1) will also 
have the task to identify (potentially) patentable results generated by the partners and ensure they are 
protected. At the end of the technical development of each use case, a specific IP study will be conducted 
in order to highlight the new knowledge acquired during the study  and to better determine the degree of 
innovation of the product or the process. When an exploitable (potentially patentable) result is identified, a 
working group of relevant partners will be established under coordination of the EIM. After a thorough study, 
suggestions will be made regarding the scope and type of the patent according to the stakes and the 
strategies of the involved partners, while keeping in mind the Consortium Agreement regulations. This IP 
study will focus on the ownership; the nature of the knowledge, and its perceived potential for exploitation; 
the agreed status of the item concerning access rights, plans to use the knowledge in exploitation, or plans 
to disseminate it outside the consortium; measures required, or in place, to ensure protection of IP for the 
item.  
Technology transfer. Since technological innovation will be generated within DECOAT, partners will be 
committed to serve as sites of technology transfer. Additionally, the Enterprise Europe Network will be used 
for technology transfer as it is the largest European Innovation Transfer Network and it reaches especially 
small businesses. The network includes chambers of commerce and industry, technology centres, 
universities and development agencies.

Website, logo and newsletter. A distinctive logo of DECOAT is already created and will be used on the 
website (will be setup and designed by OSM) and all project promotional material. The public section of the 
website will offer general information on the project and the technology area, as well as all public 
deliverables and other public documents produced in the framework of the project. Electronic newsletters 
with the progress of workflow will be available every 4 months. Special attention will be given to the quality

Continuous dissemination. Presentation of work progress of DEC OAT and of its results to the most

Dissemination campaigns (DC). An important part of this task is the implementation of the 3 DCs. These 
DCs aim to give a boost to the dissemination at specific timings over the project. More specifically the first

outside DECOAT is stimulated. Finally DC3 will serve as ‘final event’ to promote the final project results and

activities, including the press releases for DC1 and DC3. See also section 2.2.  Task 7.4 Policy input and 
standardisation - ISWA, AIMPLAS, CTB, CTAG, ECOMAT (M12-M48).  
Life Cycle Costing (LCC) performed in WP6 is an assessment of all costs related to a product or service, 
over the entire life cycle, from production over use until disposal. Thus, the economic analysis which will 
take place into DECOAT project refers not only to the cost of materials and manufacturing but also includes 
the wider implications of technology selection on project’s performance.  
Standardization activities bridge the gap between research and the introduction to the market, which will in 
turn bri ng significant economic benefits. The standardization activity within DECOAT will address: i) 
Identification of current standards that fall within the scope of the project, especially those addressing the 
“Sustainability Analysis”; ii) Identification of th e need for standardization; iii) Organization of workshops 
within identified technical committees; iv) Evaluation of how the innovative products from the project meet 
ongoing regulatory requirement such as REACH but also OECD guidance, especially those in the WPMN 
(Working Party on Manufactured Nanomaterials; e.g. Life Cycle Studies applied for nanomaterials) or in the 
WPRPW (Working Party on Resource, Productivity and Waste) (e.g. waste management of nanomaterials 
such as landfill, recycling or incineration).  
We will closely work with national and European standardisation bodies, see also the inclusion of CEN -
CENELEC, ELOT and UNE in the Advisory and Support Group. One of the DECOAT aspects that can open 
a new field of standardisation related to recycling is the definition and protocol for ‘debonding’, see also task 
2.2.2. For further acceptance and take-up by the industry such protocols are of high relevance. DECOAT is 
well-placed as several of its partners are involved in standardisation matters.

hazard and exposure data.   
• EU Nano-Safety Cluster, via partner NTUA who is chairing the Materials and Standards Working. Goal: 
share best practices, learn from other (in parallel running) projects.  
• EMCC - European Materials Characterisation Council, via partners NTUA and IRES who are in its 
Organisational Management Board. Goal: interaction for the characterisation of the nanomaterials.   
• Vision2020 – Helix on Circular Plastics: is being built by partner AIMPLAS; is expected to mobilise a 
number of stakeholders that could be relevant for / reached via DECOAT.

coordinated by IRIS, that will start fall 2018. It is dedicated to the recycling of composites and is naturally 
linked with DECOAT. Also interest to align with other projects from that call (SPIRE-10-2018) and from 
this call (NMBP -26-2018). Goal: exchange latest results & information, create synergies, search for 
common dissemination & communication activities.

This task of planning involves also the risk management, which will be carried out by considering the main

communication. The preliminary risk identification has been developed at proposal stage (see section 3.2.4) 
and will be regularly updated during the project. The assessment of risks will be developed through 
project internal workshops and surveys, with inclusion of the ASG members . The evolution of the 
identified risks as well as the early warnings from possible eme rging risks related to the new technologies 
will be constantly monitored. Strategy for monitoring and mitigating risks will be developed to support the 
coordination of the project as a whole. The identification of the risks of the project will cover the fo llowing 
areas:  
• Technological risks (specific materials and process research related barriers)  
• Market risks (market adoption and acceptance, cost/time over runs, raw material supply)  
• IPR issues and exploitation (patents and scientific knowledge management)  
• Environment, regulations and safety (challenges in Policy, Regulation and Law according)  
The overview of the DECOAT project risks will be updated regularly and will be integrated in the progress 
reports.   
Task 8.4: Data Management - IRES, OSM, ALL partners (M1-M48)   
Throughout DECOAT, large amounts of Data are expected to be generated. IRES will be responsible for 
the Design and Implementation of a solid Plan for the collection, storage, evaluation and exploitation of the 
data that will be produced during and after DECOAT. Openness, accessibility to beneficiaries and reusability 
of the produced Data will also be ensured by the Data Management Plan, in order to open the road for the 
Open Innovation Environme nt (OIE). The Data Management Plan includes all the necessary steps for 
efficient collection, safe storage, deep exploitation and evaluation of the data. These steps involve the Data 
Repository for sharing data and the Design and Implementation of a proces s, which will integrate data 
coming from different sources (Data Mapping) and securely store them. IRES will also take action for 
Metadata Handling and Sensitive Data Handling. Furthermore, Data produced throughout DECOAT will be 
shared among open European Research Databases. The project will comply with the newly imposed rules 
concerning data quality, sharing and security (also GDPR principles will be applied).

3.2 Management structure and procedures  
3.2.1 Organisational structure and the decision-making  
Since the overall consortium is not too large (16 partners) the organisational structures and the 
decision making process are kept as straightforward as possible . Both aspects are described in 
the next sections. It is of high importance not to neglect the necessary management elements to avoid 
conflicts or uncertainty about responsibilities and obligations.   
3.2.1.1 Organisational structure   
The sketch shows the structure of the 
project organisation with the arrows 
indicating the lines of communication. The 
coordinator will report directly to the EC 
Project Officer. The Project Steering 
Committee or PSC will interact with the 
coordinator who m aintains an overview of 
the project. The workpackage leaders will 
oversee the workpackages and report progress to coordinator and PSC.   
The main goals of the project coordination are: (i) organize the information flow in timely manner and 
accurately inside the consortium to meet project objectives; (ii) take the appropriate decisions to reach 
the project objectives; (iii) provide the EU with reports and organize reviews for the suitable tracking of 
the project progress. a. The Coordinator

The project will be coordinated by CTB which has a large experience with European projects. Dr Guy Buyle 
will act as project coordinator (CV in section 4), a role he also fulfilled already in FP7 projects (DECOCOAT, 
S(P)EEDKITS) and in H2020 (BIO4SELF). CTB, as coordinat or, has the overall responsibility of 
DECOAT’s project management as well as all the EU Commissions liaisons required for the proper 
operation of the project. Both CTB and members of PSC have a wide experience to handle any conflicts 
and other challenges that may occur during the lifetime of the project. The coordinator will rely on the WP 
leaders for monitoring the technical implementation of the project. He can take urgent low level decisions, 
if necessary and after discussion with the WP leaders. He can propose to the partners solutions and 
contingency plans in case of delay, discrepancies or when a technical choice has to be made. b. The 
Project Steering Committee (PSC)  
A Project Steering Committee will be installed as a supervisory body supporting the project’s normal 
operation. The PSC will supervise crucial decisions related both with all relevant administrative 
management and scientific technical matters and will be responsible of the operation of the technical work 
programmes. More specifically, PSC has a double role:  
• It is the governing body that prepares the decision for the General Assembly. It is responsible for 
proposing redistributions of funds if needed and for the management of the joint funds. Other tasks 
include approving the continuously updating and assuring agreement on the PEDR (see Task 7.1), as 
well as settling potential conflicts among partners.  
• It will assess the work within the WPs and ensure alignment of the individual WPs with the general 
DECOAT objectives. This means that the PSC is responsible for the overall management of the project. 
It will meet at least every six months. Its members can vary as the project needs, but the PSC will at 
least consist of the coordinator and the following managers:  
Quality Manager (QM) – IRES – Dr. Elias P. Koumoulos (CV in Part 4)  
The quality manager will be in charge of disseminating the quality procedures, stimulating their use and 
monitoring, with appropriate metrics, the implementation. This role will also incl ude contributing to the 
DECOAT required reporting, prvoding templates for reporting and setting up a review process, in 
collaboration with the Coordinator, to ensure proper quality of the DECOAT deliverables. Dr. Elias P. 
Koumoulos with wide experience in the field of QM will guarantee high level project deliverables. He will 
establish quality assurance into the DECOAT project through the development of a Quality Manual.   
Exploitation and Innovation Manager (EIM) – OSM - Dr. Emmanuel Sofianopoulos (CV in Part 4)  
The Project Exploitation and Innovation Manager will be responsible for ensuring the value of the project 
outcomes towards commercialisation and sustainability of the project foreground. This role is appointed to 
Mr Emmanuel Sofianopoulos from part ner OSM who is a Materials Engineer but has extensive 
professional engagement in supporting organisations towards exploiting their research results. He will use 
adequate processes and tools in order to collect the appropriate data for planning & executing the business 
plan of the project. He will also be responsible to monitor the project to guarantee consistency between 
technical and market choices. In brief he will oversee all activities related to IPR, supervise the compliance 
of all partners with the pr ovisions regarding intellectual property rights, use and dissemination laid down 
in the Consortium Agreement.   
Research & Technology Manager (RDM) – NTUA – Prof. Costas A. Charitidis (CV in Part 4)  
The Research & Technology Manager (RTM) will have an adv isory role on the R&D decisions within 
DECOAT and will ensure that the project milestones and goals are achieved. The responsibilities of RTM 
will include: determining, implementing and monitoring research and development strategies, policies and 
plans. This role is appointed to Prof. Costas Charitidis (NTUA), who has extensive R&D experience both 
as coordinator (in 5 EU projects) and partner in other European and National initiatives, dealing with high 
impact technological advancements. Prof. Costas Charitidis has served as Official External Reviewer and 
Project Technical Advisor of the European Commission (2010 -2016). His research topics include among 
others Materials Science & Nanotechnology, Nanomaterials Processing and Carbon-based Materials.   
Demonstration Manager (DM) – DEVAN – Mr Roberto Teixeira (CV in part 4).  
The Demonstration Manager will be the member of the PSC who reports on the demonstration activities. 
For this goal, the DM and the WP leader of WP5-Demonstration will work closely together. The goal of the

leaders  
The work package leaders, identified in Table 3.1b, are responsible for the day -to-day coordination and 
management of the individual WPs. This task involves:  
• Keep up to date with the technical state of the art and passing on this information to the partners where 
necessary  
• Provide guidelines to the different partners regarding their specific tasks and timing  
• Ensure work is carried out according to planning, minor deviations can be settled within a WP or among 
the concerned WP leaders and partners, larger deviations need to be reported to the PSC and 
coordinator  
• Collect the data for the review reports to be sent to the coordinator and all relevant partners  
• Prepare the progress reports in due time for the PSC and especially to the coordinator who edits and 
submits to the EC 
  Report any other important issues to the coordinator d. The General Assembly 
(GA)   
The General Assembly consists of one representative from each partner , the first person mentioned 
in the partner description (section 4). A second, proxy representative, will be designated from each 
organization in the case of absence of the first representative. The General Assembly will represent the 
highest level of decision making within the project and will decide the overall project strategy, including 
contractual matters and exploitation matters. Critical DECOAT decisions will be taken by the GA. In 
summary, the mission of the GA is: assessment of the work done; decisions about the strategy of the 
project; major decisions on technical issues; analysing technical conflicts between partners and proposing 
agreements; defaulting party management; studying the evaluation reports on all activities of all partners; 
deciding by confidential vote about allocation of finances, adding new members to the consortium, 
reviewing or amending the EU contract, change or exchange of  
WPs. Moreover, the GA will also take responsibility for th e exploitation and dissemination plan from the 
project. Meetings of the General Assembly may also be held by teleconference or other telecommunication 
means. The GA will meet 10 times:  
roughly every 6 months but with higher frequency at the beginning of D ECOAT (see also Gantt 
Chart – section 3.1.2). e. The Collaborative Work Platform (CWP)   
A dedicated internet based Collaborative Work Platform will be set up. It will provide the partners with 
all the necessary information on the project (reports, results, technical choices, publications, conferences). 
The Coordinator will be responsible for updating and dissemination of the information. The CWP dedicated 
to the project will have a public part serving the dissemination activities (see description of WP7) b ut will 
also have a protected part restricted to consortium members. The platform will contain for example the 
following functions: document centre, partners information, administrative documents. The CWP will also 
use the custom software from OSM that all ows parallel processing of databases and files. Informs 
automatically on task evolution and deliverables and creates a virtual working space for exchanging ideas 
and brainstorming. f. Advisory and Support Group (ASG)  
In order to ensure quality and industr ial relevance beyond the consortium, DECOAT established the 
Advisory and Support Group (ASG). It consists of external expert(s) who will participate as non -funded 
partners giving advice for technical developments, innovation and exploitation (in other value chains) and 
to evaluate the DECOAT work concerning the main goal of developing triggerable debonding coating 
systems and prepare their wider take up. Therefore, the ASG will also act as a bridge between the 
DECOAT (funded) project and the next phases of the development, via continuation projects and industrial 
take up. The ASG will interact with the consortium on a six-monthly basis and, where and when relevant, 
selected members of it can be asked to participate in the GA meetings. Travel costs for the AS G will be 
covered by the travel budget of the coordinator. The role of the ASG members will be to: (i) judge the 
Smart plastic materials with intrinsic recycling properties by design  
Research & Innovation Action addressing CE-NMBP-26-2018  
  
[DECOAT]    Page 89 of 70  
This proposal version was submitted by GUY BUYLE on 28/06/2018 16:55:43 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Subm ission Service. 
efficiency and effectiveness of work undertaken; (ii) ensure that the consortium is exposed to a divergent 
alternative view; (iii) introduce industrial requirements from other sectors; (iv) bring intelligence on already 
existing in the boarder scientific and technical communities.  
The ASG consists of 17 (!) members. DECOAT wants to realise a systemic innovation in the coating 
and recycling world, therefore large external support and advice from a wide range of stakeholders 
is considered a necessity. The ASG is put together with this philosophy in mind. It contains European 
associations and networks (incl. EUPC), 2 European Technology Platforms (T extile ETP, EuMaT), 
recycling and coating companies (incl. REMONDIS and DE BOER RECYCLING GROUP), a public body 
dealing with waste management (OVAM) and 3 standardisation bodies (incl. CEN -CENELEC). Also 
European Coatings, the publisher of the leading jour nal on coatings and adhesives, is included to 
guarantee DECOAT results will reach the sector. If needed, and with the approval of all DECOAT partners, 
the ASG can be further extended.  
3.2.1.2 Decision making   
The basis for all decision-making within the consortium is the Consortium Agreement (CA). As model for 
the CA, the DESCA model for companies is selected74, which was specifically developed to fit H2020 and 
which is recommended by the EC. It describes in detail all procedures related to project managem ent, 
dissemination and IPR. It will be tailored to the specific DECOAT needs once the project is approved.   
a. The General Assembly (GA) – top level   
During the General Assembly the representatives of the partners decide on important project management 
issues (see also 3.2.1.1). Before each GA meeting, partners will have to prepare a short report to be 
uploaded on the collaborative work platform. These reports should include the main results achieved by 
the partners, the main difficulties encountered and the publications and/or conference participations during 
the reporting period. These points will be discussed during the GA. Financial issues will be discussed as 
needed. The GA will also decide on IPR and exploitation routes. b. Technical Meetings – day-to-day 
decision within a WP/task  
Besides the GA there will also be interim meetings attended by a limited number of partners to address 
particular WPs, as deemed necessary. Additionally, contact among partners will be maintained by email 
or telephone, with  regular written progress reports circulated to all partners. Technical (telco) meetings 
with a reduced number of partners will be strongly encouraged to promote technical exchange and 
multidisciplinary cross training among partners. This will allow decisi on making at practical day -to-day 
level. Depending on the scope, they will be shared by the task leader or WP leader. c. Conflict 
management   
The coordinator, assisted by the PSC, will propose corrective actions if necessary, following consultation 
with GA members. If, for any reason, the coordinator and PSC cannot resolve the conflict, the GA will 
conclude on the conflict by majority vote (in c ase of draw, the coordinator has the decisive vote). For 
serious and urgent matters, an extraordinary GA can be called. d. Overview of milestones

3.2.2 Motivation for the proposed structure and decision-making process  
The WP leaders will take the lead in their respective WP and closely work together with the WP partners. 
In addition, they will not only be the contact point for the WP partners, but also for partners active in the 
other WPs. Regular contacts in between the WP leaders will therefore be organised to assure good flow 
of materials and project information.   
Besides the obvious roles for the coordinator and the WP leaders, a PSC with different managers with 
extensive expertise in scientific management, has been  established for the DECOAT project, which will 
allow a close follow-up of all crucial steps needed for a successful H2020 project. The people selected for 
the PSC are experienced and well placed to take up their role and will closely cooperate within the PSC. 
They will also be the main sparring partner for the ASG.   
The well -structured decision making process as described above (see section 3.2.1.2) will aid and 
stimulate the project progress as scheduled and avoid delays. The coordinator, in consultation with the 
respective WP leader, can take low level decisions with no or a minor impact on the other WPs and overall 
project progress. The project steering committee (see section 3.2.1.1b), completed with the required WP 
leaders, can take medium level decisions with the agreement of General Assembly. The General Assembly 
itself is responsible for all important management issues and thus takes the high level decisions.   
This overall decision-making structure is supported by well-defined deliverables and clear milestones, which 
will be closely tracked during the proposal and serve as the basis for decision points.

3.2.3 Innovation management  
The innovation management that  involves the process of 
managing an organization's innovation procedure, starting 
at the initial stage of ideation, to its final stage of 
successful implemen tation, will  ensure that there is an 
open culture for and focus on innovation in the project. We 
will ensure that ALL PARTNERS in the consortium 
understand both market and technical problems, and allow 
partners to respond to external or internal opportunit ies, and 
use its creative efforts to introduce new ideas and processes. 
This will also include promoting to use innovation management 
tools, encourage team members to undertake small -scale 
innovations that support the achievement of project objectives, 
ensure a continuous flow of new opportunities, ideas, and 
concepts that are aligned with the strategic project objectives, 
and identify new and disruptive innovation opportunities. As 
systematised complementary innovation management tools, 
we will monitor on the one hand side the novelty of our results (via technology watch and patent reviews) 
as well as track the evolution of the TRL of our results periodically to assess that they will reach the planned 
maturity in their path towards the market deployment.  
The process of innovation management has already started with the identification of the market 
opportunity that exists for recycling of coated parts, the translation of this knowledge into the 
DECOAT concept and the preliminary market analysis performed for those market sectors (see part 
‘D2’ of the PEDR in section 2.2.2(a)) that are represented by the consortium partners (i.e. outdoor gear, 
electronics consumer goods and automotive). During the more explorative R&D work (in WP1, WP2 and 
WP3) of DECOAT, the most promising results and technologies will be selected according to both their 
technical performances (basis are the target requirements defined in Task 1.1), their transferability in 
industrial scenarios (raw materials accessibility, productivity, processing requirements) and their final cost 
for industrial take -up and exploitation (investment costs, operational costs). The project management 
approach proposed provides mechanisms to identify and resolve potential risks. Accordingly, the risk 
mitigation measures reported in section 3.2.4 have been and will be selected according to their impact on 
the future and potential for the exploitation of the DECOAT results.  
Two specific aspects of the innovation management we want to highlight: (i) introducing a sy stem 
innovation; (ii) following a market pull and technology push.   
Within the project INNOQUALITY (coordinated by CTB), success factors were determined for several types 
of innovation (eg incremental, process, product or systemic innovation). The project  showed that 
introducing a systemic innovation is the most difficult because it involves all the stakeholders along the 
value chain. Within DECOAT, we will build on the experience and insights gained from INNOQUALITY for 
optimal innovation management. Further, we want to apply a combination of technology push (ie promoting 
our results) and market pull. The latter means that one addresses the end users.   
Having recognized that continuous and effective innovation management throughout and beyond the 
duration of DECOAT will be crucial for the successful deployment of the novel DECOAT technologies and 
for their introduction to the market, the consortium has (i) engaged partner OSM with specific expertise in 
innovation services; (ii) included several activities dedicated to ‘Innovation Management’ (see Tasks 7.2-
exploitation, 7.4-standardisation & policy and Task 7.5 - external liaison) and (iii) appointed an Exploitation 
& Innovation Manager as a member of the PSC (see Section 3.2.1.1b).

3.3.1  Description of the 
consortium  
  
Consortium & resources : a well -balanced mix of 17 partners from 10 different countries. Total 
budget of ca. 5.97 M€ and 812 person months for the project during of 48 months. 11 partners are 
companies (including 7 SMEs), a substantial amount of the resources will go them: ca. 55% to the 
companies, ca. 40% to the SMEs.  
Experts who hold all the 
expertise required and 
access to facilities needed 
in order to reach the 
ambitious aim of the 
DECOAT proposal have 
been chosen carefully to 
collaborate in this  
Consortium. As no single 
organization or country has 
the capacity to s uccessfully 
bring about the innovations 
and validations intended in 
DECOAT on its own, a well-
balanced consortium has 
been arranged, with 
partners that are 
complementary to each 
other and are willing to closely cooperate in creating a research environment as envisioned in DECOAT 
ambitious aims. All partners in this consortium have been selected in view of their individual expertise and 
complementarities. The project involves partners from EU members and administers the resources in 
terms of personnel, knowl edge and equipment that are required for success. This multinational 
cooperation is essential in order to reach the intended objectives.   
All partners, except for PANASONIC, have previous successful experience in multilateral collaborative 
research and have successfully worked previously in EU-funded research projects. Their resources will be 
assembled to form a coherent and synergistic project. In addition to the skills and capabilities of each of 
the DECOAT partners, each partner also represents a networ k of contacts, technology and market 
overview that in some cases is much greater than the consortium itself.  
The DECOAT consortium will be supported by the 17 members of the ASG, see section 3.2.1.1f.

3.3.2 Industrial/commercial involvement in the project  
The industrial partners form the majority in the consortium: 11 industrial organisations out of 17 partners. 
In particular 7 SMEs and 4 large enterprises, able to cover all crucial steps along the value chain, starting 
from materials synthesis and formulat ion, coating formulations, coating processes and the actual 
manufacturing of final products. These partners have been carefully selected in order to facilitate 
exploitation of DECOAT results. In fact, aiming to ensure the industrial relevance in the DECOAT project, 
we have 4 SMEs leading WP, we have 3 SMEs (out of 5 members in total) in the Project Steering 
Committee and from the total budget, ca. 55% goes to the industrial partners, more than 40% goes 
to the SMEs (see also section 3.4).  
PANASONIC is a newcomer to European collaborative projects; the other industrial partners have 
good experience from the framework, partners MAIER, DEVAN and IRIS even as coordinator of 
projects themselves. As described in 2.2, DECOAT industrial partners will also be actively involved 
in the dissemination  of results, with the end users focusing on their distributors and clients and 
technology providers on potential markets and customers. The industrial partners will also have a key role 
in the exploitation of results through the actions outlined in 2.2/D1-D3.  
Apart from the industrial partners within the project, more companies/sectors have expressed their 
interest in DECOAT either directly or through their associations (see support letters in Part 4) and will 
support the spreading and take up of DECOAT results to and by the industry via participation in the ASG 
(see section 3.2.1.1f). Members of the ASG will have access to intermediate products and processes 
guidelines, parts of the LCA/LCC studies and can be test users for the ecodesign tool etc. The goal is that 
the ASG acts also as a sound board, providing feedback and recommendations to the consortium to ensure 
that project results are relevant for applications by other users/markets, extending their exploitation beyond 
the actual duration and scope of the DECOAT project.  
3.3.3 Other countries  
All participants in the project are based in European Countries.

Partner 1 – CTB – Centexbel  
  
Country  BE  
Core Competence: coating and finishing of textiles, formulating, application on lab 
and semiindustrial scale and testing  
Brief description of legal entity:   
Centexbel (CTB) is the Belgian scientific and technical centre for the textile and plastic converting industry, 
with strong links to the majority of these companies. CTB offers a complete range of standardized testing, 
it is a notified body and can deliver  CE marking and testing. CTB is also involved in standardization 
committees and offers technological advice and training to companies in Belgium and abroad.  
The research focus of CTB is on applied research, funded by private contract as well as national a nd 
international agencies (e.g. H2020, Eranet, Interreg). Some well selected subjects for strategic research 
are: (i) finishing and coating technology; (ii) implementation of nanotechnology; (iii) intelligent textiles; (iv) 
3D textile structures via braidi ng and knitting; (v) extrusion processes and related polymer formulation 
(incl. biopolymers).  
DECOAT role and main tasks:   
• Project coordinator; leader of WP8 (coordination)  
• Leader of WP2: development of debondable coatings on textiles and their characterisation  
DECOAT specific competences and experiences:   
Centexbel has much experience in the coating and lamination of textile. In most cases these coatings are 
functionalised to obtain specific properties, e.g. recyclability.

Dr Ine De Vilder, Research scientist. G ender: F. After finishing her studies as industrial chemical

knowledge on the latest innovations in this area. One of the recent focusses of the research is the 
recyclability of coated and laminated materials and use of recycled materials as coating material.   
Dr. Guy Buyle, Manager EU research of CTB. Gender: M. Guy holds a Masters of Engineering degree

he has mainly been working on European projects, under FP6, FP7 and H2020, being strongly involved

Partner 2 – AIMPLAS - ASOCIACION DE INVESTIGACION DE MATERIALES PLASTICOS Y 
CONEXAS   
  
Country  Spain  
Core Competence: polymer materials, their transformation 
processes and recycling.  
Brief description of legal entity:   
AIMPLAS, Technological Institute of Plastics located in Valencia, is a private, non-profit Association with 
more than 500 associated companies created i n 1990. AIMPLAS is formed by +120 highly skilled 
professional, more than 65% with a Masters, Engineering or equivalent degree in Chemistry, polymer 
engineering, materials engineering or equivalent, including 15 PhD.   
AIMPLAS’ fields of work are related to technological research and development on thermoplastic and 
thermosetting plastic materials & products, its transformation processes and their recyclability and 
sustainability. AIMPLAS generates new knowledge and tech nologies that can be transferred to 
companies in order to help them to increase their effectiveness and competitiveness.  
AIMPLAS has a broad expertise in the fields of recycling, compatibilization, reactive extrusion, 
biopolymers and renewable source mate rials, special assisted processing technologies and 
nanocomposites, gained during the last years in the frame of EU and national projects. Nowadays, 
AIMPLAS is involved in more than 25 European projects and has participated in 77 projects in FP5, FP6, 
FP7, LIFE+, CIP-EcoInnovation EU Programmes, among others, coordinating 27 of them. At National and 
Regional levels AIMPLAS participates in around 100 projects yearly.   
AIMPLAS, as RTD is focused to help companies in the plastic sector to develop new products  and 
increase their competitiveness through innovation, has more than 20 pilot plants representing the most 
relevant polymer/plastics/composites production technologies present in the industry nowadays and has 
state-of-the art test facilities for chemical,  optical, morphological, mechanical and physical 
characterisation. These pilot lines and laboratories are used by many customer’s every year allowing 
them to test new materials, optimize production processes and launch new products to the market, 
supported by AIMPLAS technical staff, resulting in more than 5000 assays, 170 technical assessments 
and 120 skills training actions to more than 1500 clients per year. AIMPLAS has state-of-the-art 8500 m2 
facilities, including thermoplastics and thermoset pilot plants, analysis and testing laboratories (physical-
mechanical, chemical, packaging, automotive and construction) and training areas  
DECOAT role and main tasks:   
Selection of the components of the pilot recycling line.   
Set up and evaluation of the pilot line to recycle coated textiles and coated plastic parts for outdoor gear, 
household electronics, buses and automotive applications.   
Quality analysis of the recycled materials and evaluation of their potential use.   
DECOAT specific competences and experiences:   
AIMPLAS’ fields of work are related to technological research and development on plastic materials and 
products, their transformation processes and their recyclability and sustainability. AIMPLAS has pilot 
plants and testing laboratories that enable the full characterisation of both waste and recycled materials, 
including chemical, optical, morphological, mechanical and physical properties. It also has wide 
experience in selective separation of complex wastes, d econtamination of recycled plastics for the 
elimination of hazardous substances and/or odour, improvement of recycled properties of plastics through 
additivation and compounding, recycling of thermoplastics and elastomers, optimization of recycling 
processes and the properties of recycled plastics.

Partner 3 – IVV - Fraunhofer-Gesellschaft zur Förderung der Angewandten Forschung e. V.  
  
Country  Germany   
Core Competence: Recycling Plastics  
Brief description of legal entity:   
Fraunhofer is the leading organisation for applied research in Europe, undertaking contract research on 
behalf of industry, the service sector and government. At present, Fraunhofer has about eighty research 
units, including seventy-two research institutes, at over forty locations in Germany. An annual turnover of 
about €2300 million is generated by contract research by a staff of about twenty-five thousand employees. 
Fraunhofer’s institute für Verfahrenstechnik und Verpackung (Fraunhofer -IVV) will particip ate in this 
project:  
Fraunhofer’s Institute for Process Engineering and Packaging (Fraunhofer -IVV) has two hundred and 
twenty-one employees and an annual turnover of €18 million. The Fraunhofer-IVV develops and optimizes 
products and processes primarily i n the area of food ingredients, functional films, product safety, food 
quality, biogenic raw materials as well as plastics recycling. The department ‘Recycling polymers’ at 
Fraunhofer-IVV has been founded in 2005 and deals with the separation of pure polym ers from plastic 
containing waste by means of mechanical pre -treatment and solvent based technologies (CreaSolv® 
Process).  
DECOAT role and main tasks:   
Fraunhofer will mainly be involved in WPs 2-5. In WP2 Fraunhofer will closely interact with developers of 
triggerable debonding with respect to applied polymers and will identify suitable solvent formulations and 
conditions for coating materials. In WP3 Fraunhofer will assist automated sorting by im plementation of 
dyes which allow in -line measuring of coating thickness. Fraunhofer’s contributions to WP 4 and 5 will 
include implementation of CreaSolv® Technology in the DECOAT pilot line and its use in the course of 
demonstration.    
DECOAT specific competences and experiences:   
Fraunhofer-IVV has 20 years of experience in solvent based separation of plastic mixtures. Starting with 
laboratory scale experiments in 1996, the CreaSolv® process can now separate most thermoplastic 
materials from complex waste streams and produce recycled polymers with defined virgin-like properties, 
whereas the applied solvent is recycled completely within the process. Thus, the recycling process 
encourages the circular economy approach, as most recent project results (e.g. PolystyreneLoop) have 
shown that product qualities of recycled polymers comply with specifications of virgin plastics, enabling a 
use of recycled plastics in initial applications. Having such a technical recycling concept validated,

Process, which is upscaled in this project for the purpose of recovering POP free recycled polystyrene

Fraunhofer-IVV developed recycling processes for the recovery of polymers from polymer -metal-
composites including metal plated plastics and carbon fibre reinforced plastics. The processes reached a 
TRL of 5.  
DECOAT relevant significant infrastructure and/or major skills, equipment:   
CreaSolv® pilot plant: Fraunhofer IVV runs a flexible CreaSolv® pilot line consisting of some 100-250 L 
vessels for different unit operations like dissolution, mechanical cleaning, extractive cleaning, product 
drying and solvent recovery. In the past it was used to produce 5 -100 kg samples of – amongst others - 
ABS, PS, PC/ABS, PP, PE, PET and PA. This line has a capacity of 5-10 kg/day and will be the base of 
design studies deducing optimized process parameters for a 25 kg/h plant.

Brief description of legal entity:   
CTAG is a Spanish, private, non-profit R&D technology centre devoted to support the automotive industry 
in its research, development and innovation needs. CTAG was created in 2002 thanks to a joint initiative 
of automotive enterprises within the region.  
With a team of more than 700 prof essionals having more than 60% of international activity, CTAG is an 
ideal partner for developing new innovative products for the automotive sector using CAD product design 
and CAE simulations tools.   
CTAG is present in all the stages of product development, from initial advanced research to product life. 
The key fields of competence where CTAG concentrates its activities are: new materials, novel 
manufacturing processes, mathematical calculation and simulation, component testing and analysis of 
performances, environment, electronics, ergonomics, comfort and innovation management.   
For further information on CTAG capacities and main activities, please visit our website ( www.ctag.com) 
and check our corporative video (https://vimeo.com/120029828).  
DECOAT role and main tasks:   
WP1: Support on the definition and requirements of end-user cases on materials  
Input for WP2: Evaluation of the maximum amount of impurities allowed in the recycled material, according 
to the aimed mechanical properties, by testing different compounds with increasing amount of coating 
residue.   
WP5: Design of specifications for the material/prototype validation according to the standards an d 
protocols, development of new testing procedures if needed (depending on the functionality of the part 
selected as prototype demonstrator), characterization and validation through climate, vibration, acoustics, 
impact, fatigue, etc. testing.  
CTAG also will contribute in the supporting work packages (WP6, WP7 and WP8).  
DECOAT specific competences and experiences:   
From 2004, CTAG has a research team focused on exploring novel applications for new materials in the 
transport sector as well as enhancing the efficiency of plastic transformation processes.   
On validations side, CTAG has three buildings equipped with the ultimate testing laboratories: climatic, 
vibration & acoustics, fatigue, materials, engine, electronics and ergonomics, fitted with the cutting-edge 
technology and equipment such as two triaxial shakers integrated in acoustic and climatic chambers, 
several climatic chambers including a complete car sunlight radiation and weather resistance chamber, 
etc.

Partner 5 – NTUA – National Technical University of Athens  
  
Country  Greece  
Core Competence: NTUA is the leader of WP1 “Triggerable 
materials for coatings” and one of the key partners in synthesis, 
characterisation and processing of proposed materials. NTUA will 
develop novel smart nano- and micro-materials that will be used in 
the proposed debonding technologies.  
Brief description of legal entity:   
National Technical University of Athens (NTUA) is the oldest and most prestigious educational institution 
of Greece in the field of technology, and has contributed unceasingly to the country's scientific, technical 
and economic development since its foundation in 1836. The NTUA team comprises chemical, 
mechanical, metallurgical engineers, physicists, chemists and technicians, specialized in the fields of 
materials research and development, possessing a very experienced staff (including several professors, 
research scientists and PhD students) as well as extensive facilities for materials processing and 
characterization. R-NanoLab (http://nanolab.chemeng.ntua.gr) has all the necessary infrastructures for 
the synthesis of nano - and micro - materials. Additionally, there is the suitable equipment for the 
investigation of chemical and nanomechanical properties, as well as the surface properties and 
topographical characteristics of materials through atomic force microscopy.  
DECOAT role and main tasks:  
• Synthesis of nano-/microcapsules and smart carbonaceous hybrid nanomaterials(WP1).  
• Characterization of developed triggerable materials (WP1), coating formulations (WP2) and 
preliminary testing of specimens (WP2).  
• Support in WP3 on definition of a range of dyes to be used in the shell of the microparticles.  
• Toxicity, release and exposure assessment of nanomaterials (WP6).  
DECOAT specific competences and experiences:   
R-NanoLab (NTUA) has vast experience on the synthesis of novel stimuli-responsive nanocontainers with 
encapsulated organic substances, as well as on the synthesis and characterization of hybrid organic -
inorganic containers for coating formulations. Moreover, R -NanoLab is involved in synthesis and 
characterization of carbonace ous nanomaterials, dealing with advanced applications, such as 
antifouling/anticorrosive coatings, composite materials and smart applications, investigating also the 
toxicity and consequences of the nanoparticles.

journals have been published.
